Ruling on Buying Unseen and the Option of Sight
Commentary on the chapter of Khiyar al-Ru'ya from Kanz al-Daqaiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on buying an unseen item, explain the proof and scope of khiyar al-ru'ya, and apply the conditions and consequences.

Core Idea
Buying unseen is valid but the buyer has an option to return upon sight — a balance between freedom of contract and protection from ignorance.

This lesson examines a fundamental Hanafi doctrine in sales: the permissibility of buying an item one has not seen, coupled with a legally established option (khiyar al-ru'ya) to return it upon inspection. We will explore the primary proof from the Sunnah, the scope of this option across different contract types, and the conditions that trigger or nullify it. The commentary from Al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the nuanced positions within the school and highlights practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its proof
State the ruling: buying unseen is valid but gives the buyer an option to return upon sight. Write down the hadith from Makhul and note its evidentiary value.
2
Understand the scope of khiyar al-ru'ya
List the contracts where the option applies (purchase, lease, partition, and compromise) and where it does not (debts, dower, khul'). Note that the option is for the buyer except in salam where the seller has it.
3
Analyze the conditions for validity
Identify that the sale of an unseen item requires pointing to the item or its place. Without such indication, the sale is invalid by consensus. Distinguish between absolute permissibility (apparent from Kanz) and the qualified position of the majority.
4
Examine the effects of disposal or loss
Determine that if the buyer disposes of the item (e.g., sells it) or if it perishes, the option is void and the sale becomes binding. Conversely, if the item is returned, it is a rescission (faskh) not requiring a court order.
5
Compare with other schools
Note that Shafi'i and others generally do not recognise the option of sight unless deception occurred. This ikhtilaf shows the Hanafi emphasis on the buyer's protection against unseen defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب خيار الرؤية شراء ما لم يره جائز وله أن يرده إذا رآه وإن رضي قبله ولا خيار لمن باع ما لم يره الوصف المرغوب فيه إما أن يكون صريحاً أو دلالة لما في البدائع في خيار العيب : والجهل بالطبخ والخبز في الجارية ليس بعيب لكونه حرفة كالخياطة إلا أن يكون ذلك شرطاً في العقد، وإن لم يكن مشروطاً في العقد وكانت تحسن الطبخ والخبز في يد البائع ثم نسيت في يده فاشتراها فوجدها لا تحسن ذلك ردها لأن الظاهر أنه إنما اشتراها رغبة في تلك الصفة فصارت مشروطة دلالة وهو كالمشروط نصاً .اهـ. والله أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب. باب خيار الرؤية قدمه على خيار العيب لأنه يمنع تمام الحكم وذلك يمنع لزوم الحكم واللزوم بعد التمام والإضافة من قبيل إضافة الشيء إلى شرم رطه لأن الرؤية شرط ثبوت الخيار وعدم الرؤية هو السبب لثبوت الخيار عند الرؤية. ثم اعلم أن هذا الخيار يثبت للمشتري في شراء الأعيان ولا يثبت في الديون كالمسلم فيه والأثمان وأما في رأس مال السلم إن كان عيناً فإنه يثبت للبائع أي المسلم إليه الخيار فيه ولا يثبت في كل عقد لا ينفسخ بالرد كالمهر وبدل الخلع وبدل الصلح عن القصاص والرد بخيار الرؤية فسخ قبل القبض وبعده، ولا يحتاج إلى قضاء ولا رضا البائع وينفسخ بقوله رددت إلا أنه لا يصلح الرد إلا بعلم البائع عندهما خلافاً للثاني وهو يثبت حكماً لا بالشرط. ولا يتوقت ولا يمنع وقوع الملك للمشتري حتى إنه لو تصرف فيه جاز تصرفه وبطل خياره ولزمه الثمن، وكذا لو هلك في يده أو صار إلى حال لا يملك فسخه بطل خياره ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وذكر في المعراج أن خيار الرؤية لا يثبت إلا في أربعة أشياء : في الشراء والإجارة والقسمة والصلح عن دعوى المال على شيء بعينه . وفي المعراج : : لا يطالب البائع المشتري بالثمن قبل الرؤية قوله : (شراء ما لم يره جائز) أي قال الرملي وفي البزازية اشتراها وقبضها ثم ظهور ولادتها عند البائع لا من البائع وهو لم يعلم في رواية المضاربة عيب مطلقاً لأن التكسر الحاصل بالولادة لا يزول أبداً وعليه الفتوى. وفي رواية إن نقصتها الولادة عيب وفي البهائم ليس بعيب إلا أن يوجب نقصاناً وعليه الفتوى اهـ. فظاهر ما في البدائع أنه لا . يرد إلا إذا شرط أنها ما ولدت ولو لم يشرطه لا يرد وهو مخالف لما عليه الفتوى كما سمعت والله تعالى أعلم .اهـ. قلت ذكر في البزازية أيضاً عن النهاية باب خيار الرؤية قوله : (وأما في رأس مال السلم الخ) هكذا في بعض النسخ وفي بعضها «وأما السلم ففي كتاب البيع باب خيار الرؤية صحيح لما رواه ابن أبي شيبة والبيهقي مرسلاً عن مكحول مرفوعاً «من اشترى شيئاً لم يره فله الخيار إذا رآه إن شاء أخذه وإن شاء تركه وجهالته بعدم الرؤية لا تفضي إلى المنازعة لأنه لو لم يوافقه يرده فصار كجهالة الوصف في المعاين المشار إليه وإطلاق الكتاب يقتضي جواز البيع سواء سمي جنس المبيع أو لا، وسواء أشار إلى مكانه أو إليه وهو حاضر مستور أو لا مثل أن يقول بعت منك ما في كمي، وعامة المشايخ قالوا : إطلاق الجواب يدل على الجواز عنده . وطائفة قالوا : لا يجوز لجهالة المبيع من كل وجه والظاهر أن المراد بالإطلاق ما ذكره شمس الأئمة وصاحب الأسرار والذخيرة من أن الإشارة إليه أو إلى مكانه شرط الجواز حتى لو لم يشر إليه ولا إلى مكانه لم يجز بالإجماع مثل أن يشتري ثوباً في جراب أو زيتاً في زق أو حنطة في غرارة من غير أن يرى شيئاً، ومنه أن يقول بعتك درة في كفي صفتها كذا أو لم يقل صفتها كذا أو هذه الجارية وهي حاضرة متنقبة لبعد القول بجواز ما لم يعلم جنسه أصلاً كأن يقول بعتك شيئاً بعشرة؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وأراد بما لم يره ما لم يره وقت العقد ولا قبله، والمراد بالرؤية العلم بالمقصود من باب عموم المجاز فصارت الرؤية من أفراد المعنى المجاز ليشمل ما إذا كان المبيع مما يعرف بالشم كالمسك وما اشتراه بعد رؤيته فوجده متغيراً وما اشتراه الأعمى. وفي القنية : اشترى ما يذاق فذاقه ليلاً ولم يره سقط خياره . قوله : (وله أن . يرده إذا رآه وإن رضي (قبله أي للمشتري رده وإن قال رضيت قبل العلم به. وأعاد الضمير مذكراً للمعنى لأن الخيار معلق بالرؤية لما روينا فلا يثبت قبلها. وأورد طلب الفرق بين الفسخ والإجازة قبلها فإنها غير لازمة وهو لازم مع استوائهما في التعلق بالشرط والجواب أن للفسخ سبباً آخر وهو عدم لزوم هذا العقد، وما كان ليس بلازم فللمشتري فسخه ولم يثبت لها سبب آخر فبقيت على العدم ومنعه في فتح القدير بأنا لا نسلم أنه قبلها غير لازم بل نقول إنه بات وإنما يحصل له عدم للزوم عندها فقبلها يثبت حكم السبب وهو اللزوم .اهـ. وهو مردود لأن اللازم ما لا يقبل الفسخ من أحدهما بدون رضا الآخر وهذا يقبله إذا رآه. وفي المحيط : قيل لا يملك فسخه قبلها وقيل يملكه وهو الأصح لأن الفسخ كما يملك بالخيار يملك بسبب عدم لزوم البيع كالعارية والوديعة والوكالة والشركة وعدم اللزوم ثابت بسبب جهالة المبيع. واختلفوا هل هو مطلق أو موقت؟ فقيل موقت بوقت إمكان الفسخ بعدها حتى لو تمكن منه ولم يفسخ سقط خياره وإن لم توجد الإجازة صريحاً ولا دلالة وقيل : يثبت الخيار له مطلقاً نص عليه في نوادر ابن رستم. وذكر رأس المال إن كان الخ. قوله : (مثل أن يشتري ثوباً في جراب الخ) تمثيل لما وجد فيه شرط الجواز وقد مر في عبارة الفتح. قوله: (اشترى ما يذاق فذاقه ليلا الخ) قال الرملي : مفهومه أن ما لا يذاق لو اشتراه ليلاً لا
Chapter of Option of Sight. Buying what one has not seen is permissible, and he has the right to return it when he sees it, even if he expressed satisfaction before. There is no option for the one who sold what he has not seen. The desired description is either explicit or implicit. For in al-Badai' in the chapter of option of defect: ignorance of cooking and baking in a slave girl is not a defect because it is a skill like sewing, unless it was stipulated in the contract. If it was not stipulated and she was skilled in the seller's hand then forgot in his hand, and he bought her and found she does not do it, he returns her because the apparent indication is that he bought her desiring that quality, so it became implicitly stipulated, like an explicit stipulation. End. And Allah knows best, to Him is the return. Chapter of Option of Sight: He placed it before the option of defect because it prevents the completion of the ruling, and that prevents the bindingness of the ruling, and bindingness is after completion. The addition is like adding a thing to its condition [؟]. Because sight is a condition for the establishment of the option, and lack of sight is the cause for establishing the option upon sight. Then know that this option is established for the buyer in purchasing specific items, and is not established in debts like salam commodity and prices. As for salam capital, if it is a specific item, then the option is established for the seller, i.e., the salam recipient. It is not established in any contract that cannot be rescinded by return, like dower, khul' compensation, and compensation for compromise in lieu of qisas. Return by option of sight is rescission before and after possession. It does not require a court order or the seller's consent, and is terminated by saying 'I return it'. However, the return is only valid with the seller's knowledge according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to the second (al-Hasan). It is established by law, not by condition. It is not time-bound and does not prevent the ownership of the buyer from occurring, such that if he disposes of it, his disposal is valid, his option is void, and the price becomes binding. Similarly, if it perishes in his hand or becomes such that he cannot rescind, his option is void. As in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. It is mentioned in al-Mi'raj that the option of sight is only established in four things: purchase, lease, partition, and compromise concerning a property claim on a specific thing. And in al-Mi'raj: the seller cannot demand the price from the buyer before sight. His statement: (Buying what he has not seen is permissible) meaning ... al-Ramli said: and in al-Bazzaziyya: he bought her and took possession, then her giving birth appeared with the seller not from the seller, and he did not know; in the narration of mudaraba it is a defect absolutely because the breakage from birth never goes away, and fatwa is upon that. In another narration, if birth decreases her value it is a defect, and in animals it is not a defect unless it causes a deficiency, and fatwa is upon that. So the apparent from al-Badai' is that he only returns if he stipulated that she had not given birth; if he did not stipulate, he does not return, which contradicts the fatwa as you heard. And Allah knows best. I said: it is mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya also from al-Nihaya, chapter of Option of Sight. His statement: (And as for salam capital ...) Thus in some copies, and in some: 'And as for salam, in the book of sales, chapter of Option of Sight, it is authentic because of what Ibn Abi Shayba and al-Bayhaqi narrated as mursal from Makhul marfu'an: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen has the choice when he sees it: if he wishes he takes it, and if he wishes he leaves it.' And his ignorance due to not seeing does not lead to dispute because if it does not suit him, he returns it, so it becomes like ignorance of description in inspected items indicated. And the apparent meaning of the book (Kanz) requires the permissibility of the sale whether the genus of the item is specified or not, and whether he pointed to its place or to it while it is present but covered or not, like if he says 'I sell you what is in my sleeve.' And the majority of scholars said: the absolute answer indicates permissibility according to him (Abu Hanifa). And a group said: it is not permissible due to complete ignorance of the item. And the apparent is that the intended meaning of the absolute is what Shams al-A'imma and the author of al-Asrar and al-Dhakhira mentioned: that pointing to it or to its place is a condition for permissibility, so that if he does not point to it nor to its place, it is not permissible by consensus, like buying a cloth in a bag, oil in a skin, or wheat in a sack without seeing anything. And from it is if he says 'I sell you a pearl in my sleeve, its description is such' or does not say its description, or 'this slave girl' while she is present and veiled — because it is unlikely to say the permissibility of what one does not know its genus at all, like saying 'I sell you something for ten.' As in Fath al-Qadir. And he intended by 'what he has not seen' what he did not see at the time of the contract nor before. And the intended meaning of 'sight' is knowledge of the intended object, by way of general metaphorical usage, so that sight becomes one of the individuals of the metaphorical meaning to include when the item is known by smell like musk, and what he bought after seeing it then found it changed, and what a blind person bought. And in al-Qunyah: one who bought something that can be tasted then tasted it at night and did not see it, his option lapses. His statement: (And he has the right to return it when he sees it, even if he expressed satisfaction before) meaning the buyer can return it even if he said 'I am satisfied' before knowing it. And he made the pronoun masculine for the meaning because the option is suspended on sight as we narrated, so it is not established before it. And an objection was raised seeking the difference between rescission and acceptance before sight: the latter is not binding while the former is binding, despite both being conditional on the condition. The answer: rescission has another cause, which is that this contract is not binding. And what is not binding, the buyer can rescind it. Acceptance does not have another cause, so it remains non-existent. And this was objected in Fath al-Qadir: we do not concede that it is non-binding before sight; rather we say it is binding, and it only acquires non-bindingness at the time of sight. So before sight, the ruling of the cause applies, which is bindingness. End. But this is rejected because 'binding' is that which cannot be rescinded by one party without the other's consent, and this can be rescinded when he sees it. And in al-Muhit: it is said he cannot rescind before sight, and it is said he can, and that is the more correct, because rescission, just as it is possessed by option, is possessed due to the non-bindingness of the sale, like 'ariyya, wadi'a, agency, and partnership, and non-bindingness is established due to ignorance of the item. And they differed whether it is absolute or time-bound? Some said it is time-bound to the time when rescission is possible after sight, so that if he was able and did not rescind, his option lapses even if no explicit or implicit acceptance occurred. And some said the option is established for him absolutely, as stated in Nawadir Ibn Rustam. And he mentioned 'salam capital if it is...' His statement: (Like buying a cloth in a bag) is an example of where the condition of permissibility exists, and it has already passed in the phrase of al-Fath. His statement: (One who bought something that can be tasted then tasted it at night) al-Ramli said: its implication is that if one buys something that cannot be tasted and buys it at night, he does not...
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the chapter of Khiyar al-Ru'ya (Option of Sight) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author begins by stating the core ruling: buying something one has not seen is valid, but the buyer has the right to return it upon seeing it. This ruling is supported by a hadith narrated from Makhul: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen has the choice when he sees it, either to take it or leave it.' The ignorance caused by not seeing does not lead to dispute because the buyer can return the item if it does not suit him, similar to ignorance of description in inspected items. The author then clarifies the scope of this option: it is only for the buyer in purchases of specific items (a'yan), not debts like the salam commodity or prices. However, in salam, if the capital is a specific item, the seller (al-muslam ilayh) has the option. The option does not apply to contracts that cannot be rescinded by return, such as dower or khul' compensation. The option of sight is a rescission (faskh) both before and after possession, and it does not require a court order or the seller's consent; it is simply exercised by saying 'I return it.' It is established by law (hukman), not by condition, and it is not time-bound. Importantly, the option does not prevent ownership from passing to the buyer: if the buyer disposes of the item, the sale becomes binding and the option is lost. Similarly, if the item perishes in the buyer's hand or becomes such that he cannot return it, the option is lost. The author notes that according to al-Mi'raj, the option of sight is only established in four contracts: purchase, lease, partition, and compromise concerning a property claim on a specific thing. There is a discussion about whether the seller can demand the price before sight: he cannot. The author then discusses the conditions for the sale of an unseen item to be valid. The apparent meaning of Kanz al-Daqaiq suggests absolute permissibility, but the majority of Hanafi scholars clarify that pointing to the item or its place is a condition for validity. Without such indication, the sale is invalid by consensus. Examples include buying a cloth in a bag or oil in a skin without seeing anything. The author also defines 'what he has not seen' to include what was not seen at the time of contract or before, and 'sight' is interpreted broadly to include knowledge by other senses like smell (e.g., musk). Thus, if a blind person buys something, or if someone buys an item after seeing it but finds it changed, the option applies. A special case from al-Qunyah: if someone buys something that can be tasted and tastes it at night without seeing it, his option lapses. The passage also addresses whether the buyer can rescind before sight: the more correct view is that he can, because the contract is non-binding due to ignorance of the item. However, there is a difference of opinion on whether the option is time-bound. Some say it is time-bound to the period after sight when rescission is possible; if the buyer delays, the option lapses. Others say it is absolute, as stated in Nawadir Ibn Rustam.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The option granted to the buyer of an unseen item to return it upon sight.
الرد (al-radd): Returning the item by the buyer exercising the option of sight; it is a rescission (faskh).
الشرم (al-sharm): Unclear in text; possibly a corruption of 'الشرط' (condition) or 'شرط السبب'. Probably meaning 'condition'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer of an unseen item sells it to a third party before seeing it, what happens to his option of sight?
A) His option remains because he hasn't seen it yet.
B) His option is void and the original sale becomes binding.
C) His option is void only if he explicitly accepted after the sale.
D) His option passes to the third-party buyer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, buying an unseen item is valid with a legal option to return upon sight, but this option is lost if the buyer disposes of the item.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Establishment of the Option of Viewing (Khiyar al-Ru'ya)
Establishment and proof of khiyar al-ru'ya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khiyar al-ru'ya, explain the proof from the Companions' practice, and distinguish it from khiyar al-'ayb.

Core Idea
The buyer (and seller) may rescind an unseen sale upon seeing the item, as established by the Companions' consensus.

This lesson covers the basic ruling of khiyar al-ru'ya: when a person buys (or sells) something unseen, the contract is not binding until the item is viewed. We explore the textual proof from the incident of Sayyiduna Uthman and Sayyiduna Talha, and clarify how this option differs from the option of defect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale of an unseen item; the ruling is that the contract is not binding (ghayr lazim) until the item is seen, and the party has the option (khiyar) to rescind or confirm.
This option is established by the Lawgiver to prevent regret from ignorance.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar of Uthman and Talha: both claimed the option when cheated, and Jubayr ibn Mut'im ruled in favor of Talha (the buyer) with the Companions present, implying acceptance of the principle.
The ruling was given for Talha, but Uthman also asserted his right, so the incident supports both parties having the option.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Companions' lack of objection indicates consensus (ijma) that the option is established for both parties in principle.
The Hanafi school considers this an implicit consensus.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an abandoned statement (qawl marjoo') from Abu Hanifa that the seller has no option; the mufta bihi extends it to the seller as well.
The athar and qiyas support the seller's option because he is also a buyer of the price.
5
Distinguish from khiyar al-'ayb
If the buyer says 'I am pleased' before seeing, the option of viewing remains; but if said before knowing a defect, the option of defect is lost because the defect existed before knowledge.
The cause of khiyar al-'ayb is the defect itself, whereas the cause of khiyar al-ru'ya is the absence of sight.

كتاب البيع باب الرؤية. قال محمد في الأصل وهو الصحيح لإطلاق النص والعبرة لعين النص لا لمعناه اهـ. وحاصله أنه غير لازم قبل الرؤية بسبب جهالة المبيع وإذا رآه حدث له سبب آخر بعد لزومه وهو الرؤية ولا مانع من اجتماع الأسباب على مسبب واحد ثم اعلم أنه لا يملك فسخه إلا بعلم البائع، وقيد بخيار الرؤية لأنه لو قال وله خيار العيب رضيت به قبل أن يراه ثم رآه فلا خيار له لأن سبب الخيار فيه العيب وهو موجود قبل العلم بخلافه هنا فافترقا؛ كذا في المعراج. وفي إيضاح الإصلاح والمشتري له الخيار عنده إلى أن يوجد مبطل له وإن قال رضيت قبلها لم يقل وإن رضي قبلها لما فيه من إيهام تحقق الرضا قبلها وفساده ظاهر اهـ. ويرد قوله: (ولا خيار لمن باع ما لم يره) وهو قول الإمام المرجوع يسقط خياره إلا برؤيته ولا يشك فيه شاك، والظاهر أن النهار فيما يذاق كالليل أيضاً فيسقط خياره بذوقه من غير رؤية فلو أسقط لفظة ليلاً لكان أولى اهـ. قلت وإنما قيد به ليفيد أن مجرد الذوق فيما يذاق إذا حصل به المقصود يكفي وإن لم توجد رؤية، ويفهم بالأولى أنه إذا ذاقه نهاراً وهو يراه كفى. قوله: (وأعاد الضمير مذكراً للمعنى) أي أن حقه التأنيث لعوده إلى الرؤية لكن لما كان المراد بالرؤية العلم كما تقدم ذكر الضمير مراعاة للمعنى قوله: (ومنعه في فتح القدير بأنا لا نسلم الخ) ما بنى عليه المنع من أنه بات هو المفهوم من كلام العناية حيث تعقب الجواب المذكور بأن عدم اللزوم باعتبار الخيار فهو ملزوم الخيار والخيار معلق بالرؤية لا يوجد بدونها فكذا ملزومه لأن ما هو شرط للازم فهو شرط للملزوم. اهـ وأجاب عن هذا التعقب في الحواشي السعدية بأنا لا نسلم أن عدم لزومه للخيار بل لعدم وقوعه منبرماً. غاية ما في الباب إن عدم الانبرام باعتبار أنه يثبت له الخيار عند الرؤية وهذا لا يستلزم عدم وجوده بدونها. وقوله والخيار الخ» ممنوع لأن المعلق بالشرط يوجد قبل وجود الشرط بسبب آخر قوله: (وهو مردود الخ قال في النهر: ما ذكره هو بالرد أليق لأن الشارع حيث علق إثبات قدرة الفسخ والإجازة بالرؤية لزم القول بلزومه قبله اهـ. وهو مندفع بما مر عن الحواشي تأمل. قوله: (لأنه لو قال وله خيار العيب الواو للحال أي والحال أن له خيار العيب. إليه لأنه معلق بالشراء فلا يثبت دونه. وروي عثمان عفان بن رضي الله تعالى عنه باع أرضاً بالبصرة من طلحة بن عبيد الله فقيل لطلحة إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني اشتريت ما لم أره، وقيل لعثمان إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني بعت ما لم أره فحكما بينهما جبير بن مطعم فقضى بالخيار لطلحة وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة كذا في الهداية. وهذا الأثر رواه الطحاوي ثم البيهقي. فائدة: ذكر شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر في تقريب التهذيب جبير بن مطعم بن عدي بن نوفل بن عبد مناف القرشي النوفلي صحابي عارف بالأنساب، مات سنة ثمان أو وخمسين. ومراده البيع بثمن، أما إذا باع سلعة بسلعة ولم ير كل منهما ما يحصل له من العوض كان لكل واحد منهما الخيار لأن كل واحد منهما مشتر للعوض الذي يحصل له؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي جامع الفصولين: يثبت الخيار للبائع في الثمن لو عيناً والكيلي والوزني إذا كانا عيناً فهما كسائر الأعيان وكذا التبر من الذهب والفضة والأواني ولا يثبت خيار الرؤية فيما ملك ديناً في الذمة كالسلم والدراهم والدنانير عيناً كان أو ديناً، والكيلي والوزني لو لم يكونا عيناً فهما كنقدين لا يثبت فيهما خيار الرؤية إذا قبضا اهـ. وفي الظهيرية: لو اشترى جارية بعبد وألف فتقابضا ثم رد بائع الجارية العبد بخيار الرؤية لم ينتقض البيع في الجارية بحصة الألف وفي المحيط باع عيناً بعين لم يرها وبدين ثم رآها فردها ينتقض البيع في حصة العين ولا ينتقض في حصة الدين لأنه لا خيار في حصته اهـ. قوله: (ويبطل بما يبطل به خيار الشرط أي للمشتري يعني من صريح ودلالة وضرورة فما يفعل للامتحان لا يبطلهما إن لم يتكرر، فإن تكرر أبطلهما كالاستخدام مرة ثانية وما لا يفعل للامتحان ولا يحل في غير الملك، فإن كان ذلك التصرف لا يمكن رفعه كالإعتاق والتدبير أو تصرفاً يوجب حقاً للغير كالبيع المطلق أو بشرط خيار للمشتري والرهن والإجارة يبطله قبل الرؤية وبعدها لأنه لما لزم تعذر الفسخ فبطل الخيار، وإن كان تصرفاً لا للغير كالبيع بشرط الخيار للبائع والمساومة والهبة من غير تسليم لا يبطل قبل الرضا ويبطله بعد الرؤية لوجود دلالة الرضا ويرد عليه طلب صريح الشفعة فإنه مسقط لخيار الشرط دون خيار الرؤية هو المختار كما في الولوالجية لأنه دليل يوجب حقاً الرؤية لأنه لا يربو على قوله: (ولا يردان على صاحب الهداية أي الشفعة والعرض على البيع قوله: (فيرد على صاحب الكنز الأخذ بالشفعة) فإنه قبل الرؤية لا يبطله وكذلك قوله والبيع بخيار أي لو كان الخيار للبائع، وأما لو كان الخيار للمشتري فيبطله مطلقاً كالبيع المطلق كما مر والكلام فيما فارق خيار الشرط فكان الأولى تقييد البيع بما فيه خيار البائع. وقوله والإجارة غير صحيح فإنه يبطل خيار الرؤية أيضاً مطلقاً قبل الرؤية وبعدها كما قدمه ولعله بالزاي لا بالراء لكن يبقى مكرراً مع قوله بعد «ويرد
Book of Sale, Chapter of Viewing. Muhammad said in al-Asl: and it is the correct view due to the absolute nature of the text, and consideration is given to the literal text not its meaning, etc. Its summary: it is not binding before viewing due to ignorance of the sold item, and when he sees it, another cause arises after its binding, which is viewing, and there is no impediment to the gathering of causes upon one effect. Then know that he does not have the power to rescind except with the knowledge of the seller, and it is restricted to the option of viewing because if he said: he has the option of defect, I am pleased with it before he sees it, then he sees it, then he has no option because the cause of the option therein is the defect, which exists before knowledge, contrary to here; so they differ. As in al-Mi'raj. In Idah al-Islah: The buyer has the option with him until something that invalidates it exists, even if he said 'I am pleased' before it, he does not say 'if he is pleased before it' because of the implication that satisfaction is realized before it, and its corruption is apparent. And it is objected to by the sale with the condition of exemption from defects, for it is valid, and they said that he is pleased with all its apparent and hidden defects, and that he did not come to know them, so even if he learns of a hidden defect known only to doctors, he does not have the right to return it, so satisfaction before knowledge and viewing is possible. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: The option of viewing and the option of defect are not established in an invalid sale. In al-Muhit: He bought a waterskin full of water, so he has the option when he sees it because some water is better than others. Accordingly, he may return the water after pouring it into the jug if he had not seen it before, i.e., the jar, but it will come that if the seller carries it to the buyer's house, he is prevented from returning it unless he carries it to him. In Hiyal al-Walwaljiyya: A man sold an estate unseen by the buyer, so he wanted to sell it in a way that the buyer would not have the option of viewing. The trick is that he acknowledges a garment to some person, then sells the garment with the estate, then the acknowledgee gets the acknowledged garment, so the buyer's option is invalidated because he bought two items in one transaction and one of them is lost, so he cannot return the remainder by option of viewing because that would split the transaction against the seller. His statement: 'There is no option for one who sold what he did not see' – this is the abandoned statement of the Imam; his option is not lost except by seeing it, and there is no doubter about it. It is apparent that daytime concerning what is tasted is like nighttime, so his option is lost by tasting it without sight; so if he dropped the word 'night', it would be more appropriate. I say: He restricted it only to indicate that mere tasting in what is tasted, when the purpose is achieved, is sufficient even if sight is absent, and it is understood a fortiori that if he tastes it in daytime while seeing it, it suffices. His statement: 'He made the pronoun masculine referring to the meaning' – that is, it should be feminine because it refers back to 'viewing', but since what is meant by viewing is knowledge, as mentioned, the pronoun is masculine observing the meaning. His statement: 'He forbade it in Fath al-Qadir by saying: we do not concede, etc.' What he based the prohibition on is that it is the understanding from the words of al-Inaya, where he commented on the aforementioned answer that non-bindingness is by virtue of the option, so it is the necessary condition of the option, and the option is suspended on viewing and does not exist without it, so likewise its necessary condition, because what is a condition for the necessary condition is a condition for the necessary condition. He responded to this comment in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya by saying: we do not concede that its non-bindingness is due to the option; rather, it is due to it not being concluded. The utmost in the matter is that non-conclusion is attributed to the fact that he has the option at the time of viewing, and this does not entail its non-existence without it. And his statement 'and the option...' is denied because that which is suspended on a condition exists before the existence of the condition due to another cause. His statement: 'And it is refuted, etc.' He said in al-Nahr: What he mentioned is more deserving of refutation because the Lawgiver, when He suspended the establishment of the power of rescission and ratification on viewing, necessitates saying it is binding before it. And it is repelled by what preceded from al-Hawashi; reflect. His statement: 'because if he said: and he has the option of defect' – the waw is for the state, i.e., while the state is that he has the option of defect. To him because it is suspended on the purchase, so it is not established without it. It is narrated that Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, sold land in Basra to Talha ibn Ubaydullah, and it was said to Talha: you have been cheated. He said: I have the option because I bought what I did not see. And it was said to Uthman: you have been cheated. He said: I have the option because I sold what I did not see. So they referred to Jubayr ibn Mut'im, and he ruled in favor of Talha having the option, and that was in the presence of the Companions. So it is in al-Hidaya. This athar was narrated by al-Tahawi and then al-Bayhaqi. Benefit: Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar mentioned in Taqrib al-Tahdhib: Jubayr ibn Mut'im ibn Adi ibn Nawfal ibn Abd Manaf al-Qurashi al-Nawfali, a Companion knowledgeable in genealogies, died in the year eight or fifty-eight. And his intention is a sale for a price; but if he sells a commodity for a commodity, and neither sees what he receives as consideration, then each of them has the option because each is a buyer of the consideration he receives; so it is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: The option is established for the seller in the price if it is a specific thing, and measurable and weighable items if they are specific are like other specific items, and likewise gold and silver bullion and vessels; and the option of viewing is not established in what is owned as a debt in the dhimmah, like salam and dirhams and dinars whether specific or debt, and measurable and weighable items if they are not specific are like currency in that the option of viewing is not established in them when they are taken possession of. In al-Zahiriya: If he bought a slave girl for a slave and a thousand, and they took possession, then the seller of the slave girl returned the slave by option of viewing, the sale of the slave girl is not rescinded with respect to the portion of the thousand. In al-Muhit: He sold a specific thing for a specific thing not seen and for a debt, then he saw it and returned it, the sale is rescinded with respect to the portion of the specific thing and is not rescinded with respect to the portion of the debt because there is no option regarding its portion. His statement: 'And it is invalidated by what invalidates the option of stipulation' – i.e., for the buyer, meaning by explicit statement, indication, and necessity. So what is done for testing does not invalidate them if it is not repeated; if repeated, it invalidates them, like using (the item) a second time. And what is not done for testing and is not permissible outside of ownership – if that action cannot be reversed, like freeing and tadbir, or an action that necessitates a right for another, like an absolute sale or with a stipulation of option for the buyer, and pledge and lease, it invalidates it before viewing and after, because when it becomes binding, rescission becomes impossible, so the option is void. And if it is an action not for the other, like a sale with stipulation of option for the seller, and bargaining, and gift without delivery, it does not invalidate before satisfaction and invalidates after viewing due to the existence of indication of satisfaction. And it is objected to by the explicit demand of pre-emption, for it nullifies the option of stipulation but not the option of viewing; this is the chosen view as in al-Walwaljiyya because it is an evidence that necessitates a right – viewing because it does not increase over his statement: 'And they are not objected to by the author of al-Hidaya, i.e., pre-emption and offering for sale.' His statement: 'So it is objected to by the author of al-Kanz: taking by pre-emption' – for it does not invalidate it before viewing, and likewise his statement 'and the sale with option' – i.e., if the option is for the seller. But if the option is for the buyer, it invalidates it absolutely like an absolute sale as mentioned, and the discussion is concerning what differs from the option of stipulation, so it would have been better to restrict the sale to that which contains an option for the seller. And his statement 'and lease' is incorrect, for it invalidates the option of viewing also absolutely before and after viewing as he presented; perhaps it is with 'z' not 'r', but it remains repeated with his statement later 'wa yurad'.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the section 'Option of Viewing' (Khiyar al-Ru'ya) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The chapter discusses the ruling that the buyer (and in some cases the seller) of an item not seen at the time of contract has the right to rescind the sale upon seeing it. The author begins by stating the correct position (from Muhammad in al-Asl) that the sale is not binding before viewing due to ignorance of the subject matter. When the buyer sees the item, a new cause (the viewing) arises, and multiple causes can combine for one effect. Importantly, the buyer cannot exercise the option without informing the seller. The author then distinguishes the option of viewing from the option of defect: if the buyer says 'I am pleased' before seeing, it does not bar the option of viewing, whereas if he says so before knowing of a defect, the option of defect is lost because the defect existed before knowledge. The passage also clarifies that these options do not apply in invalid (fāsid) sales. Various examples are given, such as buying a waterskin of water – since water can vary in quality, the buyer has the option. A trick (hīla) is mentioned: if someone wants to sell an estate without giving the buyer the option of viewing, he can acknowledge a garment to another person, then sell both the garment and the estate together; the acknowledgee then takes the garment, and since the buyer bought two items in one transaction and one is lost, he cannot return the remaining item (the estate) by option of viewing as that would split the transaction against the seller. The text then discusses whether the seller also has an option when selling unseen: a report from Uthman and Talha indicates that both parties have the option, and this is confirmed by the practice of the Companions. For non-specific items like debts (e.g., dirhams in salam), the option of viewing does not apply because they are not physically seen. The passage concludes by explaining how the option of viewing is invalidated: by any action that indicates acceptance, such as using the item repeatedly, or by actions that create rights for others (like selling, pledging, leasing) which make rescission impossible. However, actions like bargaining or gift without delivery do not invalidate before satisfaction. The author also compares with option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart), noting that demand of pre-emption (shuf'a) invalidates option of stipulation but not option of viewing.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The right of a party to a sale contract to rescind the sale upon seeing the object of sale (or the price) that was unseen at the time of contract.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The right to return a defective item purchased without knowledge of the defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, if a buyer says 'I am pleased with this purchase' before seeing the item, and then later sees it and is dissatisfied, does he still have the option of viewing?
A) No, his statement indicates satisfaction and he loses the option.
B) Yes, he still has the option because satisfaction is not established until actual viewing.
C) It depends on whether the item has a defect.
D) Only if the seller agrees to allow the option.

Key Takeaway
The option of viewing is established for both parties in a sale of an unseen item, supported by the Companions' practice, and is not lost by a mere statement of satisfaction before seeing.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
What Invalidates the Option of Viewing
Rules for termination and loss of khiyar al-ru'ya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify actions that invalidate khiyar al-ru'ya and distinguish between actions that have effect before and after viewing.

Core Idea
The option of viewing is lost by actions indicating acceptance or creating irrevocable rights, similar to khiyar al-shart but with exceptions.

This lesson details the factors that terminate or invalidate khiyar al-ru'ya. We examine how explicit acceptance, using the item repeatedly, and legal acts like sale, pledge, or lease nullify the option. We also compare with khiyar al-shart and the special case of demanding pre-emption.

Guided Path
1
Categorize invalidating actions
Actions that indicate acceptance (by explicit statement, by indication, or by necessity) invalidate the option. Also actions that cannot be reversed or create rights for others.
The text mentions 'by explicit, indication, and necessity' as categories.
2
Apply to testing
Testing the item once (e.g., wearing a garment) is permissible for examination; repeating the test (using it a second time) indicates acceptance and invalidates the option.
This is specific to khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ru'ya.
3
Analyze irreversible actions
Actions like freeing a slave (itq) or tadbir (declaring freedom after death) cannot be reversed, so they nullify the option even before viewing. Similarly, selling the item to a third party, pledging, or leasing creates rights for others and invalidates the option.
Such actions make rescission impossible.
4
Compare with khiyar al-shart
Demand of pre-emption (shuf'a) invalidates khiyar al-shart but does not invalidate khiyar al-ru'ya, because the option of viewing is stronger: it arises from ignorance, not mere stipulation.
The text says 'there is no objection to the author of al-Hidaya' regarding this.
5
Apply to mixed transactions
When an item is sold with another item in one transaction, and one item is lost (e.g., by pre-emption), the option of viewing for the remaining item is lost because returning it would split the transaction.
This is from the hila example: selling a garment with the estate.

قال وله خيار العيب الواو للحال أي والحال أن له خيار العيب. إليه لأنه معلق بالشراء فلا يثبت دونه. وروي عثمان عفان بن رضي الله تعالى عنه باع أرضاً بالبصرة من طلحة بن عبيد الله فقيل لطلحة إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني اشتريت ما لم أره، وقيل لعثمان إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني بعت ما لم أره فحكما بينهما جبير بن مطعم فقضى بالخيار لطلحة وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة كذا في الهداية. وهذا الأثر رواه الطحاوي ثم البيهقي. فائدة: ذكر شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر في تقريب التهذيب جبير بن مطعم بن عدي بن نوفل بن عبد مناف القرشي النوفلي صحابي عارف بالأنساب، مات سنة ثمان أو وخمسين. ومراده البيع بثمن، أما إذا باع سلعة بسلعة ولم ير كل منهما ما يحصل له من العوض كان لكل واحد منهما الخيار لأن كل واحد منهما مشتر للعوض الذي يحصل له؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي جامع الفصولين: يثبت الخيار للبائع في الثمن لو عيناً والكيلي والوزني إذا كانا عيناً فهما كسائر الأعيان وكذا التبر من الذهب والفضة والأواني ولا يثبت خيار الرؤية فيما ملك ديناً في الذمة كالسلم والدراهم والدنانير عيناً كان أو ديناً، والكيلي والوزني لو لم يكونا عيناً فهما كنقدين لا يثبت فيهما خيار الرؤية إذا قبضا اهـ. وفي الظهيرية: لو اشترى جارية بعبد وألف فتقابضا ثم رد بائع الجارية العبد بخيار الرؤية لم ينتقض البيع في الجارية بحصة الألف وفي المحيط باع عيناً بعين لم يرها وبدين ثم رآها فردها ينتقض البيع في حصة العين ولا ينتقض في حصة الدين لأنه لا خيار في حصته اهـ. قوله: (ويبطل بما يبطل به خيار الشرط أي للمشتري يعني من صريح ودلالة وضرورة فما يفعل للامتحان لا يبطلهما إن لم يتكرر، فإن تكرر أبطلهما كالاستخدام مرة ثانية وما لا يفعل للامتحان ولا يحل في غير الملك، فإن كان ذلك التصرف لا يمكن رفعه كالإعتاق والتدبير أو تصرفاً يوجب حقاً للغير كالبيع المطلق أو بشرط خيار للمشتري والرهن والإجارة يبطله قبل الرؤية وبعدها لأنه لما لزم تعذر الفسخ فبطل الخيار، وإن كان تصرفاً لا للغير كالبيع بشرط الخيار للبائع والمساومة والهبة من غير تسليم لا يبطل قبل الرضا ويبطله بعد الرؤية لوجود دلالة الرضا ويرد عليه طلب صريح الشفعة فإنه مسقط لخيار الشرط دون خيار الرؤية هو المختار كما في الولوالجية لأنه دليل يوجب حقاً الرؤية لأنه لا يربو على قوله: (ولا يردان على صاحب الهداية أي الشفعة والعرض على البيع قوله: (فيرد على صاحب الكنز الأخذ بالشفعة) فإنه قبل الرؤية لا يبطله وكذلك قوله والبيع بخيار أي لو كان الخيار للبائع، وأما لو كان الخيار للمشتري فيبطله مطلقاً كالبيع المطلق كما مر والكلام فيما فارق خيار الشرط فكان الأولى تقييد البيع بما فيه خيار البائع. وقوله والإجارة غير صحيح فإنه يبطل خيار الرؤية أيضاً مطلقاً قبل الرؤية وبعدها كما قدمه ولعله بالزاي لا بالراء لكن يبقى مكرراً مع قوله بعد «ويرد
Book of Sale, Chapter of Viewing. Muhammad said in al-Asl: and it is the correct view due to the absolute nature of the text, and consideration is given to the literal text not its meaning, etc. Its summary: it is not binding before viewing due to ignorance of the sold item, and when he sees it, another cause arises after its binding, which is viewing, and there is no impediment to the gathering of causes upon one effect. Then know that he does not have the power to rescind except with the knowledge of the seller, and it is restricted to the option of viewing because if he said: he has the option of defect, I am pleased with it before he sees it, then he sees it, then he has no option because the cause of the option therein is the defect, which exists before knowledge, contrary to here; so they differ. As in al-Mi'raj. In Idah al-Islah: The buyer has the option with him until something that invalidates it exists, even if he said 'I am pleased' before it, he does not say 'if he is pleased before it' because of the implication that satisfaction is realized before it, and its corruption is apparent. And it is objected to by the sale with the condition of exemption from defects, for it is valid, and they said that he is pleased with all its apparent and hidden defects, and that he did not come to know them, so even if he learns of a hidden defect known only to doctors, he does not have the right to return it, so satisfaction before knowledge and viewing is possible. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: The option of viewing and the option of defect are not established in an invalid sale. In al-Muhit: He bought a waterskin full of water, so he has the option when he sees it because some water is better than others. Accordingly, he may return the water after pouring it into the jug if he had not seen it before, i.e., the jar, but it will come that if the seller carries it to the buyer's house, he is prevented from returning it unless he carries it to him. In Hiyal al-Walwaljiyya: A man sold an estate unseen by the buyer, so he wanted to sell it in a way that the buyer would not have the option of viewing. The trick is that he acknowledges a garment to some person, then sells the garment with the estate, then the acknowledgee gets the acknowledged garment, so the buyer's option is invalidated because he bought two items in one transaction and one of them is lost, so he cannot return the remainder by option of viewing because that would split the transaction against the seller. His statement: 'There is no option for one who sold what he did not see' – this is the abandoned statement of the Imam; his option is not lost except by seeing it, and there is no doubter about it. It is apparent that daytime concerning what is tasted is like nighttime, so his option is lost by tasting it without sight; so if he dropped the word 'night', it would be more appropriate. I say: He restricted it only to indicate that mere tasting in what is tasted, when the purpose is achieved, is sufficient even if sight is absent, and it is understood a fortiori that if he tastes it in daytime while seeing it, it suffices. His statement: 'He made the pronoun masculine referring to the meaning' – that is, it should be feminine because it refers back to 'viewing', but since what is meant by viewing is knowledge, as mentioned, the pronoun is masculine observing the meaning. His statement: 'He forbade it in Fath al-Qadir by saying: we do not concede, etc.' What he based the prohibition on is that it is the understanding from the words of al-Inaya, where he commented on the aforementioned answer that non-bindingness is by virtue of the option, so it is the necessary condition of the option, and the option is suspended on viewing and does not exist without it, so likewise its necessary condition, because what is a condition for the necessary condition is a condition for the necessary condition. He responded to this comment in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya by saying: we do not concede that its non-bindingness is due to the option; rather, it is due to it not being concluded. The utmost in the matter is that non-conclusion is attributed to the fact that he has the option at the time of viewing, and this does not entail its non-existence without it. And his statement 'and the option...' is denied because that which is suspended on a condition exists before the existence of the condition due to another cause. His statement: 'And it is refuted, etc.' He said in al-Nahr: What he mentioned is more deserving of refutation because the Lawgiver, when He suspended the establishment of the power of rescission and ratification on viewing, necessitates saying it is binding before it. And it is repelled by what preceded from al-Hawashi; reflect. His statement: 'because if he said: and he has the option of defect' – the waw is for the state, i.e., while the state is that he has the option of defect. To him because it is suspended on the purchase, so it is not established without it. It is narrated that Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, sold land in Basra to Talha ibn Ubaydullah, and it was said to Talha: you have been cheated. He said: I have the option because I bought what I did not see. And it was said to Uthman: you have been cheated. He said: I have the option because I sold what I did not see. So they referred to Jubayr ibn Mut'im, and he ruled in favor of Talha having the option, and that was in the presence of the Companions. So it is in al-Hidaya. This athar was narrated by al-Tahawi and then al-Bayhaqi. Benefit: Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar mentioned in Taqrib al-Tahdhib: Jubayr ibn Mut'im ibn Adi ibn Nawfal ibn Abd Manaf al-Qurashi al-Nawfali, a Companion knowledgeable in genealogies, died in the year eight or fifty-eight. And his intention is a sale for a price; but if he sells a commodity for a commodity, and neither sees what he receives as consideration, then each of them has the option because each is a buyer of the consideration he receives; so it is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: The option is established for the seller in the price if it is a specific thing, and measurable and weighable items if they are specific are like other specific items, and likewise gold and silver bullion and vessels; and the option of viewing is not established in what is owned as a debt in the dhimmah, like salam and dirhams and dinars whether specific or debt, and measurable and weighable items if they are not specific are like currency in that the option of viewing is not established in them when they are taken possession of. In al-Zahiriya: If he bought a slave girl for a slave and a thousand, and they took possession, then the seller of the slave girl returned the slave by option of viewing, the sale of the slave girl is not rescinded with respect to the portion of the thousand. In al-Muhit: He sold a specific thing for a specific thing not seen and for a debt, then he saw it and returned it, the sale is rescinded with respect to the portion of the specific thing and is not rescinded with respect to the portion of the debt because there is no option regarding its portion. His statement: 'And it is invalidated by what invalidates the option of stipulation' – i.e., for the buyer, meaning by explicit statement, indication, and necessity. So what is done for testing does not invalidate them if it is not repeated; if repeated, it invalidates them, like using (the item) a second time. And what is not done for testing and is not permissible outside of ownership – if that action cannot be reversed, like freeing and tadbir, or an action that necessitates a right for another, like an absolute sale or with a stipulation of option for the buyer, and pledge and lease, it invalidates it before viewing and after, because when it becomes binding, rescission becomes impossible, so the option is void. And if it is an action not for the other, like a sale with stipulation of option for the seller, and bargaining, and gift without delivery, it does not invalidate before satisfaction and invalidates after viewing due to the existence of indication of satisfaction. And it is objected to by the explicit demand of pre-emption, for it nullifies the option of stipulation but not the option of viewing; this is the chosen view as in al-Walwaljiyya because it is an evidence that necessitates a right – viewing because it does not increase over his statement: 'And they are not objected to by the author of al-Hidaya, i.e., pre-emption and offering for sale.' His statement: 'So it is objected to by the author of al-Kanz: taking by pre-emption' – for it does not invalidate it before viewing, and likewise his statement 'and the sale with option' – i.e., if the option is for the seller. But if the option is for the buyer, it invalidates it absolutely like an absolute sale as mentioned, and the discussion is concerning what differs from the option of stipulation, so it would have been better to restrict the sale to that which contains an option for the seller. And his statement 'and lease' is incorrect, for it invalidates the option of viewing also absolutely before and after viewing as he presented; perhaps it is with 'z' not 'r', but it remains repeated with his statement later 'wa yurad'.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the section 'Option of Viewing' (Khiyar al-Ru'ya) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The chapter discusses the ruling that the buyer (and in some cases the seller) of an item not seen at the time of contract has the right to rescind the sale upon seeing it. The author begins by stating the correct position (from Muhammad in al-Asl) that the sale is not binding before viewing due to ignorance of the subject matter. When the buyer sees the item, a new cause (the viewing) arises, and multiple causes can combine for one effect. Importantly, the buyer cannot exercise the option without informing the seller. The author then distinguishes the option of viewing from the option of defect: if the buyer says 'I am pleased' before seeing, it does not bar the option of viewing, whereas if he says so before knowing of a defect, the option of defect is lost because the defect existed before knowledge. The passage also clarifies that these options do not apply in invalid (fāsid) sales. Various examples are given, such as buying a waterskin of water – since water can vary in quality, the buyer has the option. A trick (hīla) is mentioned: if someone wants to sell an estate without giving the buyer the option of viewing, he can acknowledge a garment to another person, then sell both the garment and the estate together; the acknowledgee then takes the garment, and since the buyer bought two items in one transaction and one is lost, he cannot return the remaining item (the estate) by option of viewing as that would split the transaction against the seller. The text then discusses whether the seller also has an option when selling unseen: a report from Uthman and Talha indicates that both parties have the option, and this is confirmed by the practice of the Companions. For non-specific items like debts (e.g., dirhams in salam), the option of viewing does not apply because they are not physically seen. The passage concludes by explaining how the option of viewing is invalidated: by any action that indicates acceptance, such as using the item repeatedly, or by actions that create rights for others (like selling, pledging, leasing) which make rescission impossible. However, actions like bargaining or gift without delivery do not invalidate before satisfaction. The author also compares with option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart), noting that demand of pre-emption (shuf'a) invalidates option of stipulation but not option of viewing.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option that one or both parties stipulate to have for a specified period, during which they can confirm or rescind the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following actions does NOT invalidate the option of viewing before the buyer has seen the item?
A) Freeing the purchased slave (itq).
B) Selling the item to a third party.
C) Offering the item for sale (not actually selling) but not concluding the deal.
D) Pledging the item as collateral.

Key Takeaway
The option of viewing is lost by actions indicating acceptance or by irreversible actions that make rescission impossible, but testing once and actions without delivery do not invalidate before viewing.

Definition and Proof of the Option of Inspection
Establishes khiyar al-ru'yah with hadith and scope regarding property types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah, identify its proof from the Companions, and apply the distinctions between 'ayn and dayn to determine when the option is available.

Core Idea
A buyer or seller who has not seen the countervalue may rescind the contract upon inspection—based on the precedent of the Companions.

In this lesson, we explore the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) in Hanafi sales law. You'll learn that this option is not limited to the buyer; the seller also enjoys it when the price is unseen. The primary evidence comes from a famous incident involving two Companions, 'Uthman and Talha, and the ruling of Jubayr ibn Mut'im in their presence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the ruling being established? The option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) gives a party who has not seen the countervalue the right to rescind the contract upon seeing it.
This is a discretionary right (haqq), not a fard or wajib.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The narration of 'Uthman and Talha: 'Uthman sold land to Talha; both were told they were defrauded. They appointed Jubayr ibn Mut'im as arbitrator, who ruled in favor of Talha in the presence of the Companions.
This is a Sunnah ahad report, transmitted by al-Tahawi and al-Bayhaqi.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Jubayr's ruling and the lack of objection indicate acceptance of the option for the buyer. 'Uthman's statement 'I have the option because I sold what I did not see' extends the option to the seller as well, though the case ruled only for the buyer.
The Hanafi school uses this precedent to grant both parties the option.
4
Understand the scope
The option applies only to specific identified objects ('ayn), not to debts (dayn) in the dhimmah. In cash sales, only the buyer has the option (since the price is usually dayn). In barter, both parties have the option.
Distinctions from Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Zahiriyyah.
5
Apply to mixed sales
If a sale involves both an 'ayn and a dayn, the option of inspection applies only to the 'ayn portion; rescission is partial.
Example from al-Muhit: selling a specific object for a specific object plus a debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب خيار الرؤية
إليه لأنه معلق بالشراء فلا يثبت دونه، وروي عثمان عفان بن رضي الله تعالى عنه باع أرضاً بالبصرة من طلحة بن عبيد الله فقيل لطلحة إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني اشتريت ما لم أره ، وقيل لعثمان إنك قد غبنت فقال لي الخيار لأني بعت ما لم أره فحكما بينهما جبير بن مطعم فقضى بالخيار لطلحة وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة كذا فـي ا في الهداية . وهذا الأثر رواه الطحاوي ثم البيهقي.
سبع
فائدة : ذكر شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر في تقريب التهذيب جبير بن مطعم بن عدي بن نوفل بن عبد مناف القرشي النوفلي صحابي عارف بالأنساب، مات سنة ثمان أو وخمسين. ومراده البيع بثمن، أما إذا باع سلعة بسلعة ولم ير كل منهما ما يحصل له من العوض كان لكل واحد منهما الخيار لأن كل واحد منهما مشتر للعوض الذي يحصل له؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي جامع الفصولين : يثبت الخيار للبائع في الثمن لو عيناً والكيلي والوزني إذا كانا عيناً فهما كسائر الأعيان وكذا التبر من الذهب والفضة والأواني ولا يثبت خيار الرؤية فيما ملك ديناً في الذمة كالسلم والدراهم والدنانير عيناً كان أو ديناً، والكيلي والوزني لو لم يكونا عيناً فهما كنقدين لا يثبت فيهما خيار الرؤية إذا قبضا اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : لو اشترى جارية بعبد وألف فتقابضا ثم رد بائع الجارية العبد بخيار الرؤية لم ينتقض البيع في الجارية بحصة الألف وفي المحيط باع عيناً بعين لم يرها وبدين ثم رآها فردها ينتقض البيع في حصة العين ولا ينتقض في حصة الدين لأنه لا خيار في حصته اهـ .
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option of Inspection. It is dependent on the purchase and does not exist without it. It is narrated that 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, sold land in Basra to Talha ibn 'Ubayd Allah. It was said to Talha: 'You have been defrauded.' He said: 'I have the option because I bought what I did not see.' And it was said to 'Uthman: 'You have been defrauded.' He said: 'I have the option because I sold what I did not see.' So they appointed Jubayr ibn Mut'im as arbitrator between them, and he ruled in favor of Talha. That was in the presence of the Companions, as mentioned in al-Hidayah. This tradition is narrated by al-Tahawi and then al-Bayhaqi. A benefit: Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar mentioned in Taqrib al-Tahdhib that Jubayr ibn Mut'im was a Companion knowledgeable in genealogy, died in the year eight or fifty-eight. And his intent is sale for a price. But if one sells a commodity for a commodity and each does not see what he receives as compensation, each has the option because each is a buyer of the compensation he receives; as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: The option is established for the seller regarding the price if it is a specific object. Items measured by volume or weight, if they are specific, are like other specific objects. Likewise, bullion of gold and silver and vessels. The option of inspection is not established for what is owned as a debt in the dhimmah, such as salam, dirhams, and dinars, whether specific or debt. Items measured by volume or weight, if they are not specific, are like currencies—no option of inspection is established for them when received, end quote. In al-Zahiriyyah: If one buys a slave girl for a slave and one thousand and they take possession, then the seller of the slave girl returns the slave by option of inspection, the sale of the slave girl is not rescinded regarding the portion of the thousand. In al-Muhit: If one sells a specific object for a specific object not seen, and a debt, then sees it and returns it, the sale is rescinded regarding the portion of the specific object and not rescinded regarding the portion of the debt because there is no option in its portion, end quote.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It defines the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) and presents the primary evidence from the practice of the Companions. The option is contingent upon the sale contract; it does not arise independently. The well-known incident of 'Uthman and Talha establishes that both the buyer and seller have the option when they have not seen the object of sale or the price. Jubayr ibn Mut'im's ruling in favor of Talha, in the presence of the Companions without objection, serves as an authoritative precedent. The passage then clarifies scope: in a cash sale, only the buyer has the option; in a barter sale, both parties have it because each is a buyer of the compensation. It further distinguishes types of property. The option applies to specific identified objects ('ayn), including bullion and vessels. It does not apply to debts (dayn) in the dhimmah, such as salam contracts or currency, regardless of whether the currency is specific or generic. Items measured by volume or weight, if not specific, are treated like currency—no option after receipt. The passage concludes with two rulings from al-Zahiriyyah and al-Muhit: in mixed sales involving both specific goods and debts, the rescission is partial only for the portion where the option applies.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): An option of inspection that allows a party who has not seen the object of sale or the price to rescind the contract upon seeing it.
عين ('ayn): A specific, identified object (as opposed to a debt or obligation in the dhimmah).
دين في الذمة (dayn fi al-dhimmah): A debt obligation owed in the abstract, not tied to a specific object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which type of sale does the option of inspection apply to both the buyer and the seller?
A) A cash sale where the buyer has not seen the goods.
B) A barter sale where neither party has seen the countervalue.
C) A sale of a debt (dayn) in the dhimmah.
D) A sale of currency where the buyer has not seen the coins.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ru'yah is a right for any party who has not seen the countervalue, based on the practice of the Companions, and applies to specific objects ('ayn) but not to debts.

Actions That Void the Option of Inspection vs Condition
Critical comparison of voiding actions for two options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish which actions void khiyar al-ru'yah versus khiyar al-shart and apply the principle that actions indicating consent void the option after sight.

Core Idea
Many actions void the option of condition but not the option of inspection — the key is whether the action indicates consent after seeing.

The option of inspection allows the buyer to rescind after seeing the item. But certain actions can waive this right. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq meticulously enumerates which actions void the option and how they differ from the option of condition. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying the rulings of khiyar al-ru'yah in sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two options compared
Recognize that the passage contrasts khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection) with khiyar al-shart (stipulated option). Note that some actions affect both, some only one.
The default principle: after sight, any action indicating consent voids the option of inspection; before sight, only explicit consent voids it.
2
Categorize actions by effect on third parties and reversibility
Actions are classified as: (1) creating irrevocable third-party rights (e.g., sale, emancipation, pledge, lease) – void both options absolutely; (2) reversible actions without third-party impact (e.g., sale with option for seller, gift without delivery) – void only after sight; (3) testing actions (e.g., using once) – do not void unless repeated.
Irreversible actions void even before sight because the contract becomes binding.
3
Note the specific exceptions for khiyar al-shart
Actions like requesting pre-emption (shuf'ah), offering to sell (ard al-bay'), and letting without rent (iskan bila ujr) void the option of condition but NOT the option of inspection. Understand the rationale: they indicate consent but are not as strong as explicit consent after sight.
This is a key practical distinction: the option of inspection is more resilient.
4
Apply the overarching principle of consent
After sight, any action that clearly indicates consent (dalil al-rida) voids the option of inspection. Before sight, only explicit verbal consent (sarih) voids it. Use this to evaluate any new case.
The commentator defends the author of al-Hidayah by arguing that apparent consent before sight is not sufficient.
5
Address post-sight physical handling
If the buyer takes delivery or pays the price after sight, the option is voided. But if the seller transports the item to the buyer's house, the buyer may return it only to the contract location – transportation costs are borne by the buyer.
This aligns with the rule that the option is lost once the buyer exercises ownership rights.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) that discusses in detail what actions void the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) as compared to the option of condition (khiyar al-shart). The author systematically examines actions categorized by whether they are for testing, whether they are reversible, and whether they create rights for others. Actions done solely for testing (like handling or using once) do not void the option; but if repeated, they indicate consent and void it. Irreversible acts (like emancipation) or acts that create third-party rights (like a sale, pledge, or lease) void the option both before and after seeing because the contract becomes binding. Acts that do not affect others (like selling with an option for the seller, bargaining, or gift without delivery) do not void before seeing but void afterward as a sign of consent. The passage then engages in a critical dialogue with previous authorities, particularly the authors of al-Kanz and al-Hidayah, pointing out inconsistencies and offering resolutions. Specific rulings are given: pre-emption request and offer to sell void only the option of condition, not inspection; lease voids both; letting without rent voids only condition. The passage also addresses the effect of post-sight actions: delivery of price, transport of goods, planting by a tenant, and loss of the option if it once lapses. The overall principle is that any action indicating consent (rida) after sight voids the option, but before sight only explicit consent voids it.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): An option of inspection that allows a party to rescind upon seeing the sold item or price.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option within a sale agreement allowing a party to rescind within a specified period.
دلالة الرضا (dalalat al-rida): An action that implicitly indicates consent, as opposed to explicit verbal consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions voids the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) but NOT the option of condition (khiyar al-shart)?
A) Letting the property without rent.
B) Requesting pre-emption (shuf'ah).
C) Selling the item to a third party.
D) Emancipating a slave purchased.

Key Takeaway
The option of inspection is more resilient than the option of condition; actions indicating consent void it only after sight, while many actions void the condition option even before sight.

Implicit Consent and Its Effect on Options: Khiyar al-Shart vs. Khiyar al-Ru'yah
Explaining that actions indicating consent nullify option of condition but not option of sight before sight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effects of implicit consent before sight on Khiyar al-Shart and Khiyar al-Ru'yah, and apply the Hanafi rule to scenarios involving offering for sale, leasing, and renting.

Core Idea
Before sight, actions indicating consent cancel the option of condition but not the option of sight.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores a critical distinction in Hanafi sales law: how actions that imply acceptance (like offering the item for sale) affect two different types of options. The commentator defends the general rule that implicit consent nullifies Khiyar al-Shart (the stipulated option) but not Khiyar al-Ru'yah (the option of sight) before the buyer has seen the item. You will learn the nuances and the objections addressed by the author.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two options and their nature
Khiyar al-Shart is a contractual option based on a condition; Khiyar al-Ru'yah is a legal right to return an unseen item after seeing it. Recognize that each has different sensitivity to consent before sight.
The passage focuses on actions before the buyer has actually seen the item.
2
State the general rule from the matn
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq asserts that explicit consent (صريح الرضا) does not nullify Khiyar al-Ru'yah before sight. Therefore, implicit consent (دلالة الرضا) is even less effective and also does not nullify it. However, implicit consent does nullify Khiyar al-Shart.
The rule is a first awla (all the more reason) argument.
3
Examine the qiyas reasoning
The analogy is: explicit consent (e.g., saying 'I accept') does not nullify Khiyar al-Ru'yah before sight. Implicit consent (like offering for sale) is a weaker form of consent, so it also cannot nullify Khiyar al-Ru'yah. This supports the distinction.
This is a clear Qiyas Jali where the illa is the nature of consent.
4
Analyze the specific actions and objections
The text discusses actions like offering for sale (العرض على البيع), renting without rent (الإسكان بغير أجر), and selling with option (البيع بخيار). It shows how these actions before sight only nullify Khiyar al-Shart, not Khiyar al-Ru'yah. Objections from other Hanafi sources (e.g., al-Hidayah) are addressed.
Actions after sight (like taking possession or paying price) nullify both options.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that implicit consent before sight nullifies only Khiyar al-Shart. The option of sight remains intact until the buyer actually sees the item and performs an overt act of acceptance (like taking possession).
This is the consistent Hanafi view maintained by the later scholars.

كتاب البيع باب خيار الرؤية تعیب مع أنه الرضا وصريحه لا يبطله فدلالته أولى كالعرض على البيع وأخواته وهذا هو العذر للمؤلف لأنه قدم أن صريح الرضا لا يبطله ،قبلها، ولا يرد أن على صاحب الهداية لأنه قال من وتصرف كما في العناية لكن يرد عليه الإسكان بغير أجر فإنه مبطل لخيار الشرط فقط تصرف ويرد عليه الزيادة فإنها تبطلهما. والحاصل أن كلاً من العبارتين لم يسلم من الإيراد فيرد على صاحب الكنز الأخذ بالشفقة والعرض على البيع والبيع بخيار والإجارة والإسكان بلا أجر فإنها تبطل خيار الشرط دون الرؤية، وهذه لا ترد على صاحب الهداية إلا الإسكان فإنه تصرف ولكن يرد عليه ما في جامع الفصولين لو أسكن المشتري في الدار رجلاً بلا أجر سقط خيار الشرط كما لو أسكن بأجر، وفي خيار الرؤية لا يسقط إلا إن أسكنه بأجر اهـ. ولم يقيد بكونه قبل الرؤية ويرد على الكلية أيضاً الرضا به قبل الرؤية لا يبطله ويبطل خيار الشرط، وأما العرض على البيع فقدمنا أنه لا يبطله قبلها ويبطله بعدها والقبض أو نقد الثمن بعد الرؤية مسقط له
Book of Sales, Chapter on Option of Sight. ... defect with that consent and its explicit form does not nullify it, so its indication is more appropriate, like offering for sale and its like, and this is the excuse for the author because he stated that explicit consent does not nullify it before it. And it is not refuted against the author of al-Hidayah because he said 'who acts' as in al-Inayah, but it is refuted by renting without rent, for it nullifies the option of condition only, acting, and by increase, for it nullifies both. Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe discussing the rule that actions indicating consent (like offering for sale) have different effects on the option of condition (خيار الشرط) and the option of sight (خيار الرؤية). The author defends the general statement from the matn against criticisms, clarifying that before sight, implicit consent nullifies the option of condition but not the option of sight. The text engages with objections raised against the authors of al-Kanz and al-Hidayah, showing that certain actions like showing the goods for sale, leasing, or renting without rent after sight nullify the option of sight, but before sight they do not. The discussion emphasizes the subtlety of timing and the distinction between explicit and implicit consent.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option of sight; the right of the buyer to return an unseen item after seeing it if it does not meet his satisfaction.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of condition; a stipulated period during which either party may cancel the sale.
الرضا (al-rida): Consent or approval, either explicit (صريح) or implicit (دلالة).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Before sight, implicit consent (such as offering for sale or renting without rent) cancels the option of condition but not the option of sight; the option of sight remains until the buyer has actually seen the item.
